<div id="review_151546738" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151546738" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2293285-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516920167p2/2293285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151546738?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/2293285-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781444001839" href="/book/show/9789800-my-sister-lives-on-the-mantelpiece">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2293285-emma?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151546738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17373022986759094472"> My mum loved this book. It's rare she says she loves a book, and she's a bigger reader than me. So I think I expected big, cry-inducing, things from this book. So I’m just gonna put this out there- I didn’t love this book. <br/><br/> I remember reading books like these when I was a child, where these children have less than perfect childhoods for whatever reason and I never understood their actions or reasons for thinking the way they did. So there you have it, I didn’t ‘get’ the story. <br/><br/> I found the book</span>
  <span id="freeText17373022986759094472" style="display:none"> My mum loved this book. It's rare she says she loves a book, and she's a bigger reader than me. So I think I expected big, cry-inducing, things from this book. So I’m just gonna put this out there- I didn’t love this book. <br /><br /> I remember reading books like these when I was a child, where these children have less than perfect childhoods for whatever reason and I never understood their actions or reasons for thinking the way they did. So there you have it, I didn’t ‘get’ the story. <br /><br /> I found the book a bit of an effort to read without wanting to throw it down annoyance. I know it's a YA book and I'm reading it with an adult's perspective, but I remember being Jamie's age clearly. I remember my 10th birthday too, which wasn't a barrel a laughs either, and I remember understanding things more than Jamie seemed to. But then I suppose your emotional growth will be stunted with parents like his.<br /><br /> We meet Jamie just as he is about to move to the Lake District with his Dad and sister, Jasmine. The family have been falling apart since Jasmine’s twin sister, Rose, is killed by a terrorist bomb and Jamie’s Mum has left them to be with someone else. With his Dad drinking too much, Jamie hopes this move will change things for the better.<br /><br /> When he gets to the Lake District, nothing changes. His Dad keeps drinking, Jasmine is never around and the only seat left in his new class at school is next to a Muslim girl, Sunya. He feels like he’s betraying his Dad by sitting next to her, and then she becomes his best friend.<br /><br /> The whole story is from Jamie’s point of view and sees him coping with very adult issues because his parents have selfishly stopped being parents and have started obsessing over themselves because they lost a child, meanwhile forgetting they’ve still got two other children that need loving and protection. Jamie thinks that in doing certain things that it will bring his Mum back and make his Dad stop drinking, not completely realising that it’s beyond his control. Sunya, in some form of understanding what was happening to him, tries to make his life a little better by being his friend, even when Jamie, at first, repeatedly tries to keep her away from him.<br /><br /> Whilst I wanted to see this story for what it was- how a family copes after something as devastating as this- I couldn’t. I kept blindsided with anger towards the parents of Jamie and Jasmine and I take my hat off to Annabel Pitcher for that. She may not have gotten my love for this story, but she certainly got my respect for making me feel so angry about these characters that I wanted to just shake them and tell them that Rose wasn’t their only child. Not many people can make me feel so passionately like that, even if I wasn’t uplifted by the story.<br /><br /> I cannot deny that Pitcher can write a story that makes you feel a range of emotions though, so I look forward to seeing what she comes up with in future books, but this one is definitely not a keeper for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17373022986759094472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1129067381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129067381" />
    <a title="Rita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3285400-rita"><img alt="Rita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388657592p2/3285400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129067381?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rita" href="/user/show/3285400-rita">Rita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781780621869" href="/book/show/18301604-my-sister-lives-on-the-mantelpiece">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3285400-rita?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3285400-rita?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3285400-rita?shelf=100-book-challenge-2014">100-book-challenge-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3285400-rita?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129067381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer472677474457043340">After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/804802880?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ketchup Clouds</a> by Annabel Pitcher, I was recommended to read <i>My Sister Lives on the Mantelpiece</i> by her as well. And I'm glad that I did.<br/><br/>This is a sad and heart-wrenching story about a ten-year-old boy and his wondrous and innocent view on his life and the ones surrounding him.<br/><br/>Jamie was an adorable character; he sometimes didn't get the deeper meaning of what his sister or his friend said to him and I would get frustrated in some scenarios, but it was understandable. He was ten year</span>
  <span id="freeText472677474457043340" style="display:none">After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/804802880?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Ketchup Clouds</a> by Annabel Pitcher, I was recommended to read <i>My Sister Lives on the Mantelpiece</i> by her as well. And I'm glad that I did.<br /><br />This is a sad and heart-wrenching story about a ten-year-old boy and his wondrous and innocent view on his life and the ones surrounding him.<br /><br />Jamie was an adorable character; he sometimes didn't get the deeper meaning of what his sister or his friend said to him and I would get frustrated in some scenarios, but it was understandable. He was ten years old, so I cut him some slack. He wanted to make everyone around him happy and he tried his best at school so that his parents would be proud of him and care for him and not only for his dead sister, who lived on the mantelpiece.<br /><br />Jas was a great sister. I loved her pink hair, her sassiness, her toughness in such a situation, her boyfriend with green spiky hair, her love for Jamie.<br /><br />Sunya was also a great character. How she didn't resent Jamie like the other kids did, how she wanted to be his friend, being a superhero.<br /><br />Jamie's parents were horrible. They were up to their necks in their grief about their lost daughter that they didn't even realise that they had two other children who were still alive. This drove me mad and I loathed them. But especially Jamie's father went through a character growth and I was happy how he turned out by the end of the book.<br /><br />The premise was interesting and I wanted to know how and why and what would happen in the story. I loved the diversity, the cat, the characters.<br /><br />I cried at the end because it got so emotional, I just couldn't hold back.<br /><br />I also loved how this story ended. Not perfect, but on a positive and realistic note.<br /><br />Great, great story with awesome, but also flawed characters. I definitely would recommend this book to everyone who likes to read emotional and/or contemporary books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="472677474457043340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_973415586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/973415586" />
    <a title="Beth Bonini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3106785-beth-bonini"><img alt="Beth Bonini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444482564p2/3106785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/973415586?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Bonini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Bonini" href="/user/show/3106785-beth-bonini">Beth Bonini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=children-s-book-club">children-s-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer973415586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7608676427479606039">This book is difficult to classify. Technically, it is a children's book; it has a 10 year old narrator, and the story is told entirely from his point-of-view. And yet, I'm more apt to describe this book as YA -- or "for everyone" who has grown up and had to deal with all of the losses, big and small, that life throws at you. (That should cover pretty much <b>everyone</b>.) <br/><br/>Young Jamie has had to deal with loss on a spectacularly huge scale. His sister has died in a terrorist bombing five years before </span>
  <span id="freeText7608676427479606039" style="display:none">This book is difficult to classify. Technically, it is a children's book; it has a 10 year old narrator, and the story is told entirely from his point-of-view. And yet, I'm more apt to describe this book as YA -- or "for everyone" who has grown up and had to deal with all of the losses, big and small, that life throws at you. (That should cover pretty much <b>everyone</b>.) <br /><br />Young Jamie has had to deal with loss on a spectacularly huge scale. His sister has died in a terrorist bombing five years before the book begins. His parents' marriage has split up. He and his teenage sister Jas (twin of the dead sister) have been moved from London to the Lake District with their alcoholic father who is barely coping. Jas has dyed her hair pink and is suffering from anorexia. School is a hostile place, and the only person who seems to want to befriend Jamie is a young Muslim girl called Sunura (also an outcast). Unfortunately, Jamie's father actively nurtures a pathological hatred for all Muslims since the death of his daughter, so even this sweet friendship is fraught with feelings of guilt and betrayal.<br /><br />So, having read the full plate of misfortune that Jamie is having to deal with, would you still be willing to read on? What saves the book, and makes it possible for a sensitive reader to cope with, is Jamie's voice -- which, thankfully, has many wonderful qualities and only a partial understanding of the above described horrors. He is the classic "naive" narrator "who reveals the flaws and the faults of the world around him through his own inexperience and innocence." What an underdog; what a sweetheart. You can't help but root for him and feel for him and desperately hope for his life to turn a corner. And just so you know, there IS a happy ending (albeit of the most gentle and realistic sort).</span>
  <a data-text-id="7608676427479606039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7634071660552461897">Five years after the city-wide terrorist bombing attacks in London, one family of a victim continues to deal with the consequences. The family is a victim also with mum leaving for another man, the father sunk in booze, the dead girl's 15 year old twin going Goth and the 10 year old narrator facing a new school, confusion in choices to be made and massive bullying.<br/>The author has done a brilliant job in producing a 10 year old awkward boy with red hair, zero friends, little sporting prowess and f</span>
  <span id="freeText7634071660552461897" style="display:none">Five years after the city-wide terrorist bombing attacks in London, one family of a victim continues to deal with the consequences. The family is a victim also with mum leaving for another man, the father sunk in booze, the dead girl's 15 year old twin going Goth and the 10 year old narrator facing a new school, confusion in choices to be made and massive bullying.<br />The author has done a brilliant job in producing a 10 year old awkward boy with red hair, zero friends, little sporting prowess and full of day dreams. It's a clever story line to have him find friends with another loner - the only Muslim girl in the class. His father blames all Muslims for killing his daughter, his classmates hate anyone different and the class teacher is straight from the conservative 50s with a behavioural chart that maps each child's progress to heaven.<br />A massive tick from me.</span>

<div id="review_1194950573" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194950573" />
    <a title="Rona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4253494-rona"><img alt="Rona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599775659p2/4253494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194950573?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rona" href="/user/show/4253494-rona">Rona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781445886831" href="/book/show/13068707-my-sister-lives-on-the-mantelpiece">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4253494-rona?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4253494-rona?shelf=other-voices">other-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4253494-rona?shelf=interfaith">interfaith</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4253494-rona?shelf=good-on-cd">good-on-cd</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194950573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17033778560412817209">The story begins five years after the death of a ten year old girl from a terrorist bomb. The family is falling apart. The now-ten-year-old son tells us -- to the best of his ten-year-old understanding -- what has happened to his parents, his sister, and himself in the wake of this tragic event.<br/>I wish this was a story of love and redemption. It is, but it's not. It is a story of a family muddling through.<br/>The author did an extraordinary job of capturing the interior life of a little boy who grapp</span>
  <span id="freeText17033778560412817209" style="display:none">The story begins five years after the death of a ten year old girl from a terrorist bomb. The family is falling apart. The now-ten-year-old son tells us -- to the best of his ten-year-old understanding -- what has happened to his parents, his sister, and himself in the wake of this tragic event.<br />I wish this was a story of love and redemption. It is, but it's not. It is a story of a family muddling through.<br />The author did an extraordinary job of capturing the interior life of a little boy who grapples with his spotty memories of his lost sister, his spotty understanding of the behavior of adults in his life, his bond with his parentified older sister (now 15), and his struggles with the school bully. He befriends a Muslim girl and struggles to balance his loyalty to her with his loyalty to his lost sister (and his hateful father.) <br />He also struggles, as ten-year-old do, with the simplified religious teachings he is getting at his parochial school. There is laughable pediatric Catholicism. There is also cringe-worthy blind anti-Muslim hate.<br />I don't usually cry when I read books. This one brought me to uncontrollable sobs at two points. I had family loss early. Because of this, I note that the author did an exceptional job of capturing the confusion, the guilt of limited memory, the magical thinking, the expectation that adults can handle things dashed by the realization that they can't, and the inability to make order out of what is a chaotic family life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17033778560412817209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y0EbPYGpFk5+Y7oNAk77PnEarBocjlIgojbT9/ZxhWkMq28AI/7/rOrTIWXNJ2LyXiLjO/M8hcfQ5cejofiBQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lvs1FKJquf86zbPwfhv7Q7Ma3YM8xSwePU6G1su/4zr5EUEpAD1QHa59KJixcmKPnCKSotN3+/lPnZKCnDbnEA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

descarnada, sin concesiones, pero llena también de emoción y ternura, y que gira en torno a dos temas esenciales y universales: la muerte y la memoria.\n Es también una novela valiente, con la pretensión de ser un canto al ser humano y lo más sublime de su esencia, a su capacidad de sobreponerse a la desgracia y de enfrentar el conocimiento de sí mismo.<\/span>\n  <a Para calmar a la pequeña, el autor de La metamorfosis se inventó una peculiar historia: la muñeca no se había perdido, se había ido de viaje, y él, convertido en cartero de muñecas, tenía una carta que le llevaría al día siguiente al parque. Según cuenta Dora Dymant, su compañera en aquellos días, el estado febril con el que Kafka escribía esas cartas era comparable al de cualquiera de sus inmortales obras. Éste es el relato de aquella experiencia, en la que Franz Kafka fue un mago de la palabra para una niña desconocida de la que jamás volvió a saberse nada, como tampoco de aquellas cartas que       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4388883.Annabel_Pitcher">About Annabel Pitcher</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9078605497297856613">Annabel Pitcher studied English at Oxford and has since worked as a script writer and an English teacher. She lives in Yorkshire with her husband. MY SISTER LIVES ON THE MANTELPIECE was her first novel. She is a full-time writer.</span>
